                  <hi rend="ital">He endeavoured to turn him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">convert him, to El-Islám;</hi> occurring in a trad., in which the agent of the verb is Mohammad, and the object is his uncle Aboo-Tálib;. syn. <foreign lang="ar">رَاجَعَهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رَادَّهُ</foreign>: (L:) or <foreign lang="ar">رَاوَدْتُهُ عَلَى كَذَا</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى الأَمْرِ</foreign>, (Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مُرَاوَدَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رِوَادٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) [primarily] signifies <hi rend="ital">I desired,</hi> (S, Msb, K, *) or <hi rend="ital">sought,</hi> (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">of him that he should do such a thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the thing;</hi> (S, * Msb;) <foreign lang="ar">المُرَاوَدَةُ</foreign> implying contention (<foreign lang="ar">المُخَاصَمَة</foreign>), because he who desires, or seeks, affects gentle, or bland, behaviour, like him who deceives, or beguiles, and, like him, strives, or labours, to attain his object: (Msb:) and [hence,] <foreign lang="ar">راودهُ عَنِ الأَمْرِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْهِ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He endeavoured to turn him by blandishment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by deceitful arts,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to entice him to turn, from the thing,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">to it;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">دَارَاهُ</foreign>, (M, L,) or <foreign lang="ar">رَادَاهُ</foreign>.                   <hi rend="ital">Walk thou,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">go thou, gently,</hi> &amp;c.: (T, A:) so accord. to the lexicologists [in general]: but accord. to Sb, it is a verbal n.: [for] they said, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17038-4" target="رُوَيْدَ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>زَيْدًا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Act thou gently, softly,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a leisurely manner, towards,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with, Zeyd;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">grant him a delay,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">respite; let him alone,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">leave him, for a while;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَمْهِلْهُ</foreign>: hence it has no dual nor pl. nor fem. form: and hence they say that it is for <foreign lang="ar">إِرْوَادًا</foreign>, in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">أَرْوِدْ</foreign>; as though it were an abbreviated dim., formed by the rejection of the augmentative letters: this is the opinion of Sb; for he holds it to be a substitute for <foreign lang="ar">أَرْوِدْ</foreign>; though it has a nearer resemblance to <foreign lang="ar">إِرْوَادٌ</foreign> because it is a noun: others hold it to be the dim. of <foreign lang="ar">رُودٌ</foreign>, and cite the saying [of a poet], <quote>

                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">As though he were like him who walks,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goes, gently,</hi> &amp;c.]: but this is a mistake; for <foreign lang="ar">رُودٌ</foreign> is not put in the place of a verb, as <foreign lang="ar">إِرْوَادٌ</foreign> is. (M.) Accord. to Ibn-Keysán,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17038-5" target="رُوَيْد" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> seems to have two contr. significations; for they said, <foreign lang="ar">رُوَيْدَ زَيْدًا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Leave thou Zeyd,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">let him alone;</hi> and also meaning <hi rend="ital">act thou gently towards,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with, Zeyd, and retain him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">withhold him.</hi> (TA.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n17038-6" target="رُوَيْدَكَ" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>عَمْرًا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Act thou gently,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">towards,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with, 'Amr;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَمْهِلْهُ</foreign>: (T, * S, M, * K:) the <foreign lang="ar">ك</foreign> in this case being a denotative of allocution, (T, S, M,) and having no place in the desinential syntax: (S, M: *) it is added only when <foreign lang="ar">رويد</foreign> is used in the sense of an imperative; (T, S, K;) and to prevent confusion of him who is meant to be addressed with him who is not meant, because <foreign lang="ar">رويد</foreign> applies to one and to more than one and to the male and to the female; though sometimes one says <foreign lang="ar">رويدك</foreign> to a person when one does not fear his being confounded with another, using the <foreign lang="ar">ك</foreign> as a corroborative.       <foreign lang="ar">سَارَ القَوْمُ <ref cref="n17038-18" target="رُوَيْدًا" n="18" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party, went,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">journeyed, going,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">journeying, gently,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">leisurely</hi>]; it being here in connection with a determinate noun, and therefore a denotative of its state.
